<script type="application/ld+json">{"@context":"https:\/\/schema.org","@type":"BlogPosting","headline":"Threat Assessment: Ignoble Scorpius, Distributors of BlackSuit Ransomware","name":"Threat Assessment: Ignoble Scorpius, Distributors of BlackSuit Ransomware","description":"Explore this assessment on cybercrime group Ignoble Scorpius, distributors of BlackSuit ransomware. Since May 2023, operations have increased \u2014affecting critical sectors.","url":"https:\/\/unit42.paloaltonetworks.com\/threat-assessment-blacksuit-ransomware-ignoble-scorpius\/","mainEntityOfPage":"https:\/\/unit42.paloaltonetworks.com\/threat-assessment-blacksuit-ransomware-ignoble-scorpius\/","datePublished":"November 20, 2024","articleBody":"Executive Summary\r\nUnit 42 researchers have observed an increase in BlackSuit ransomware activity beginning in March 2024 that suggests a ramp up of operations. This threat emerged as a rebrand of Royal ransomware, which occurred in May 2023. Unit 42 tracks the group behind this threat as Ignoble Scorpius. Since the rebrand, Unit 42 has observed at least 93 victims globally, a quarter of which were in the construction and manufacturing industries.\r\n\r\nThe group describes themselves as an \u201cextortioner named BlackSuit\u201d and claims to reverse file encryption for \u201cquite a small compensation essentially.\u201d Although the group states the compensation is small, Unit 42 has observed that, on average, the initial ransom demand is about equal to 1.6% of the victim organization\u2019s annual revenue. As of the date of this report, the median victim revenue across all industries is roughly $19.5 million, making the ransom payout quite significant for all organizations.\r\n\r\nThis threat assessment includes details identified during routine threat research activities, incident response cases and collaboration with the Unit 42 Managed Threat Hunting team.\r\n\r\nThis report maps the group\u2019s activity to the MITRE ATT&amp;CK\u00ae framework in that section, which organizations can use to assess their coverage of threats posed by Ignoble Scorpius, pre- and post-compromise.\r\n\r\nPalo Alto Networks customers are better protected from the threats discussed above through the following products:\r\n\r\n \tThe Unit 42 Managed Threat Hunting and Managed Detection and Response teams conduct proactive hunts for pre- and post-incident activity.\r\n \tCortex XDR and XSIAM block and alert on known techniques and files associated with Ignoble Scorpius. We provide XQL queries in the MITRE ATT&amp;CK TTPs section of this report.\r\n \tPalo Alto Networks Next-Generation Firewalls with cloud-delivered security services, including Advanced WildFire, detect known malicious files associated with Ignoble Scorpius.\r\n \tOrganizations can engage the Unit 42 Incident Response team to help with a compromise or to provide a proactive assessment to lower your risk.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nRelated Unit 42 Topics\r\nBlackSuit Ransomware, Royal Ransomware, Ignoble Scorpius\r\n\r\n\r\nRelated Unit 42 Themes\r\nCybercrime, Ransomware\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nBlackSuit Ransomware Overview\r\nBlackSuit ransomware emerged in May 2023 as a rebrand of the Royal ransomware. Unit 42 Threat Intelligence assesses that the group behind this threat is a direct evolution of Royal, and as such we track the group under the same moniker, Ignoble Scorpius.\r\n\r\nMuch like the operations as Royal ransomware, BlackSuit operates a dark web leak site where they publish their victims\u2019 names and stolen data to extort them into paying a ransom. Figure 1 shows an excerpt of this site.\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_137589\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"1999\"] Figure 1. Screenshot of BlackSuit leak site.[\/caption]\r\n\r\nSince the rebrand, Unit 42 has observed at least 93 victims globally and an upward trend in the number of successful compromises shared on their leak site. This suggests an overall ramping up of operations. Figure 2 below details the monthly total leak site posts from Ignoble Scorpius as BlackSuit.\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_137581\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"900\"] Figure 2. Activity from Ignoble Scorpius under the BlackSuit name, May 2023 through October 2024.[\/caption]\r\n\r\nThe number of organizations truly impacted by the group is likely higher, as organizations can pay their ransom before ransomware operators post details on their leak sites to avoid reputational damage.\r\n\r\nThe median revenue of these victims was $19.5 million, which highlights the average size of organizations that the group has successfully targeted. Based on ransom negotiations observed by Unit 42, we can also estimate that the group\u2019s initial ransom demand is equal to about 1.6% of the victim organization\u2019s annual revenue.\r\n\r\nBreaking down the 93 victims by sector indicates a preference for the education, construction and manufacturing sectors, as shown in Figure 3 below.\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_137583\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"900\"] Figure 3. Pie chart breakdown of Ignoble Scorpius victimology.[\/caption]\r\n\r\nFinally, as with many ransomware groups, Ignoble Scorpius\u2019 victims are overwhelmingly based in the United States, as shown below in Figure 4.\r\n\r\n[caption id=\"attachment_137585\" align=\"alignnone\" width=\"900\"] Figure 4. Ignoble Scorpius\u2019 geographical impact.[\/caption]\r\nAttack Lifecycle\r\nThe following sections highlight tactics, techniques and procedures (TTPs) observed from Ignoble Scorpius during BlackSuit incident response investigations Unit 42 conducted. Similar findings have also been shared by researchers at ReliaQuest and The DFIR Report.\r\nInitial Access\r\nInitial access for Ignoble Scorpius, and ransomware groups in general, can be highly varied due to the prevalence of initial access brokers (IABs) who sell stolen credentials or other forms of access to organizations. While some threat actors obtain initial access on their own, others require the expertise of IABs to gain entry into a compromised network.\r\n\r\nDuring an incident response investigation, delineating between the TTPs of a suspected IAB or the ransomware group is not always possible. Within Ignoble Scorpius\u2019 ransomware cases, Unit 42 has observed many different initial access methods, including:\r\n\r\n \tPhishing campaigns with malicious email attachments (T1566.001);\r\n \tSEO poisoning with GootLoader (T1608.006);\r\n \tUsing legitimate VPN credentials (T1078), potentially obtained via social engineering and voice-based phishing (aka vishing) of executives (T1566.004)\r\n \tA software supply chain attack (T1195.002).\r\n\r\nCredential Access and Privilege Escalation\r\nUnit 42 has observed Ignoble Scorpius using common credential theft tools, such as Mimikatz and NanoDump, which is \u201ca flexible tool that creates a minidump of the LSASS process.\u201d Techniques observed include:\r\n\r\n \tDumping LSASS via Taskmgr (T1003.001)\r\n \tPerforming a DCSync attack (T1003.006)\r\n \tUsing Impacket to conduct an adversary-in-the-middle (AiTM) attack (T1557)\r\n \tRequesting Kerberos service tickets (T1558.002)\r\n\r\nOnce they have obtained sufficiently privileged accounts (i.e., domain administrator on Windows systems) Ignoble Scorpius has been observed dumping the NTDS.dit file via ntdsutil, (T1003.003) to compromise the domain controller.\r\nLateral Movement\r\nUnit 42 has observed Ignoble Scorpius making use of RDP (T1021.001), SMB (T1021.002) and PsExec (T1570) to move laterally across systems.\r\nDefense Evasion\r\nUnit 42 has observed Ignoble Scorpius and other ransomware groups making use of a vulnerable driver and loader, which are called STONESTOP and POORTRY by Mandiant. They use these tools to disable and evade antivirus and EDR solutions (T1562.001).\r\nExfiltration\r\nIgnoble Scorpius has used various commonly available software and services to exfiltrate victim data. We observed WinRAR and 7-Zip being used to compress and stage files prior to exfiltration, after which attackers used WinSCP over FTP and Rclone to exfiltrate files. In at least one instance, attackers renamed Rclone to svchost.exe prior to execution (T1048).\r\n\r\nUnit 42 has also observed Ignoble Scorpius using a third-party project management application named Bublup to exfiltrate files (T1567, T1567.002). Threat actors often abuse, take advantage of or subvert legitimate products for malicious purposes. This does not imply that the legitimate product is flawed or malicious.\r\nExecution and Impact\r\nAs Ignoble Scorpius' goal is to encrypt and ransom a victim\u2019s files, the primary payload of their campaigns is the BlackSuit ransomware. During incident response investigations involving BlackSuit, Unit 42 has also observed attackers using other tools for persistent access and the execution of arbitrary commands.\r\n\r\nThese additional tools include Cobalt Strike and SystemBC. In these cases it was not possible to identify whether Ignoble Scorpius or an IAB deployed the tools.\r\n\r\nThe final ransomware payload has Windows and Linux operating system variants with specific functionality to target VMware ESXi servers in some Linux variants.\r\nWindows Variant\r\nUnit 42\u2019s analysis of the Windows variant found that the execution of the malware required the command-line argument -id followed by a 32-character value. The ID identifies the victim and grants access to a private chat room on Ignoble Scorpius' dark website to negotiate the ransom. They provide the ID to the victim via the ransom note. An example ransom note is shown below:\r\nGood whatever time of day it is!\r\n\r\nYour safety service did a really poor job of protecting your files against our professionals.\r\n\r\nExtortioner named BlackSuit has attacked your system.\r\n\r\nAs a result all your essential files were encrypted and saved at a secure server for further use and publishing on the Web into the public realm.\r\n\r\nNow we have all your files like: financial reports, intellectual property, accounting, law actions and complaints, personal files and so on and so forth.\r\n\r\nWe are able to solve this problem in one touch.\r\n\r\nWe (BlackSuit) are ready to give you an opportunity to get all the things back if you agree to make a deal with us.\r\n\r\nYou have a chance to get rid of all possible financial, legal, insurance and many others risks and problems for a quite small compensation.\r\n\r\nYou can have a safety review of your systems.\r\n\r\nAll your files will be decrypted, your data will be reset, your systems will stay in safe.\r\n\r\nContact us through TOR browser using the link:\r\n\r\nhxxp[:\/\/]weg7sdx54bevnvulapqu6bpzwztryeflq3s23tegbmnhkbpqz637f2yd[.]onion\/?id=[ID]\r\nOther command-line arguments for the Windows variant of BlackSuit malware are shown below in Table 1.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nArgument\r\nFunctionality\r\n\r\n\r\n-path\r\nSpecifies a target directory to encrypt\r\n\r\n\r\n-id\r\nVictim ID\r\n\r\n\r\n-ep\r\nPercentage of a file that should be encrypted\r\n\r\n\r\n-localonly\r\nEncrypts only the local system\r\n\r\n\r\n-networkonly\r\nEncrypts file shares connected to the system\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nTable 1. BlackSuit Windows variant command-line arguments.\r\n\r\nAnalysis of BlackSuit ransomware from TrendMicro and SentinelOne in 2023 identified more command-line flags than recent samples. This could be due to the ransomware group creating variants that target ESXi servers specifically, which we detail below, or a consolidation of functionality.\r\n\r\nAfter the initial execution, the malware creates a mutual exclusion flag (aka mutex) with the value Global\\WLm87eV1oNRx6P3E4Cy9 to prevent machines from being infected multiple times. As a result, the mutex chosen by Ignoble Scorpius needs to be a unique value that is not frequently changed. Unit 42 has observed attackers using this mutex as recently as June 2024, with open source highlighting its use as early as October 2023.\r\n\r\nTo ensure the encryption of as many files as possible, the ransomware enumerates and terminates a list of known processes and services (T1057). The ransomware also uses Windows Restart Manager (rstrtmgr.dll) to identify processes using files that would prevent encryption, terminating anything that isn't a critical process or the Windows File Explorer (explorer.exe). This is a technique commonly used by ransomware payloads.\r\n\r\nThe malware uses the following command to delete shadow backups (T1490):\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nTo execute the ransomware payload, researchers at ReliaQuest observed Ignoble Scorpius downloading VirtualBox and creating a virtual machine (VM) (T1564.006). They copied the ransomware payload from the VM using PsExec (T1570) to \u201chundreds of hosts via SMB\u201d (T1021.002). They then used Windows Management Instrumentation Command-line (WMIC) to load the ransomware as a library to execute it. This is a technique that Unit 42 has also observed from the group (T1047, T1218.010).\r\n\r\nThey then enumerate available files (T1083) and encrypt them using OpenSSL AES, adding the extension .blacksuit to the encrypted file\u2019s name (T1486).\r\nESXi Variant\r\nThe ESXi variant, a Linux-based executable, targets virtual machines and introduces two more command-line flags:\r\n\r\n \t-vmkill (shuts down virtual machines before encryption if set)\r\n \t-crypt_all\r\n\r\nIf the -crypt_all flag is not set, the following files relating to VMware are encrypted:\r\n\r\n \t*.vmsd\r\n \t*.vmx\r\n \t*.vmxf\r\n \t*.vmdk\r\n \t*.vmem\r\n \t*.vmsn\r\n \t*.nvram\r\n \t*.vmx~\r\n \t*.vswp\r\n \t*.vmtx\r\n \t*.vmss\r\n\r\nConclusion\r\nOur analysis indicates that BlackSuit is a direct continuation of the activity under Royal, and as such we have opted to continue tracking the group under the same identifier as Royal \u2013 Ignoble Scorpius. The true effectiveness of rebranding is difficult to quantify. However, it can offer ransomware groups a respite from the scrutiny of researchers, law enforcement and the media.\r\n\r\nA more subtle effect of rebranding is the perception it can have on defenders. For example, BlackSuit\u2019s predecessor Royal and their predecessor Conti were some of the most reported and sophisticated ransomware groups while active.\r\n\r\nAs a result, organizations who were looking to assess their exposure to ransomware at the time could have looked toward the most prolific ransomware groups and attempted to cater their defensive solutions toward them. Rebranding resets this perception, and if it is accompanied with a shift in the group\u2019s TTPs, it can place defenders on their back foot.\r\n\r\nThis is one of the primary reasons we chose to highlight Ignoble Scorpius\u2019 BlackSuit ransomware in this report. Although the group as BlackSuit might not yet reach the top 10 list of ransomware groups by number of compromises, this group has the following qualities:\r\n\r\n \tThey conduct complex supply chain attacks\r\n \tThey exhibit a high level of sophistication compromising at least 93 organizations without a public-facing RaaS program\r\n \tTheir membership likely includes members from Conti and Royal ransomware\r\n\r\nThis report maps the group\u2019s activity to the MITRE ATT&amp;CK framework in the that section below. Organizations can use this information to assess their coverage of threats posed by Ignoble Scorpius, pre- and post-compromise.\r\nProtections and Mitigations\r\nPalo Alto Networks customers are better protected from the threats discussed above through the following products:\r\n\r\n \tThe Unit 42 Managed Threat Hunting and Managed Detection and Response teams conduct proactive hunts for pre- and post-incident activity.\r\n \tCortex XDR and XSIAM block and alert on known techniques and files associated with Ignoble Scorpius. We provide XQL queries in the MITRE ATT&amp;CK TTPs section of this report.\r\n \tPalo Alto Networks Next-Generation Firewalls with Cloud-Delivered Security Services, including Advanced WildFire, detect known malicious files associated with Ignoble Scorpius.\r\n\r\nIf you think you may have been compromised or have an urgent matter, get in touch with the Unit 42 Incident Response team or call:\r\n\r\n \tNorth America Toll-Free: 866.486.4842 (866.4.UNIT42)\r\n \tEMEA: +31.20.299.3130\r\n \tAPAC: +65.6983.8730\r\n \tJapan: +81.50.1790.0200\r\n\r\nPalo Alto Networks has shared these findings with our fellow Cyber Threat Alliance (CTA) members. CTA members use this intelligence to rapidly deploy protections to their customers and to systematically disrupt malicious cyber actors. Learn more about the Cyber Threat Alliance.\r\nAdditional Resources\r\n\r\n \tBlackSuit Attack Analysis \u2013 ReliaQuest Threat Research Team\r\n \tBlackSuit Ransomware \u2013 The DFIR Report\r\n \tThreat Actor Spotlight: BlackSuit Ransomware \u2013 Arete Incident Response\r\n \t#StopRansomware: Blacksuit (Royal) Ransomware \u2013 Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency (CISA)\r\n\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTPs\r\nTable 2 below depicts the MITRE ATT&amp;CK TTPs mapping for techniques referenced in this report.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nID\r\nTactic\r\nTechnique Name\r\nProcedure\r\n\r\n\r\nT1570\r\nLateral Movement\r\nLateral Tool Transfer\r\nUses PsExec for lateral movement and tool transfer\r\n\r\n\r\nT1567.002\r\nExfiltration\r\nExfiltration Over Web Service: Exfiltration to Cloud Storage\r\nUses RClone and Bublup for data exfiltration\r\n\r\n\r\nT1566.004\r\nInitial Access\r\nPhishing: Spearphishing Voice\r\nUses vishing with executives\r\n\r\n\r\nT1566.001\r\nInitial Access\r\nPhishing: Spearphishing Attachment\r\nSends phishing emails using malicious attachments\r\n\r\n\r\nT1564.006\r\nDefense Evasion\r\nHide Artifacts: Run Virtual Instance\r\nUses VirtualBox to create virtual machines\r\n\r\n\r\nT1562.001\r\nDefense Evasion\r\nImpair Defenses: Disable or Modify Tools\r\nVulnerable drivers\/loaders used to disable and evade antivirus and EDR solutions\r\n\r\n\r\nT1558.004\r\nCredential Access\r\nSteal or Forge Kerberos Tickets: AS-REP Roasting\r\nUses toolkits such as Rubeus to compromise accounts using AS-REP roasting\r\n\r\n\r\nT1558.003\r\nCredential Access\r\nSteal or Forge Kerberos Tickets: Kerberoasting\r\nUses toolkits such as Rubeus to compromise accounts using Kerberoasting\r\n\r\n\r\nT1558.002\r\nCredential Access\r\nSteal or Forge Kerberos Tickets: Silver Ticket\r\nRequests Kerberos service tickets\r\n\r\n\r\nT1557\r\nCollection, Credential Access\r\nAdversary-in-the-Middle\r\nUses Impacket to conduct AitM attacks\r\n\r\n\r\nT1490\r\nImpact\r\nInhibit System Recovery\r\nDeletes shadow copies using a specific vssadmin.exe command\r\n\r\n\r\nT1486\r\nImpact\r\nData Encrypted for Impact\r\nFiles are encrypted with the .blacksuit file extension\r\n\r\n\r\nT1218.010\r\nDefense Evasion\r\nSystem Binary Proxy Execution: Regsvr32\r\nWMIC used to load the ransomware as a library, executing it through regsvr32.exe\r\n\r\n\r\nT1195.002\r\nInitial Access\r\nSupply Chain Compromise: Compromise Software Supply Chain\r\nUses supply chain compromise for initial access\r\n\r\n\r\nT1189\r\nInitial Access\r\nDrive-by Compromise\r\nSearch engine optimization (SEO) poisoning with GootLoader\r\n\r\n\r\nT1140\r\nDefense Evasion\r\nDeobfuscate\/Decode Files or Information\r\nUses stack strings to obfuscate data\r\n\r\n\r\nT1110\r\nCredential Access\r\nBrute Force\r\nConducted brute-force attacks against virtual private network (VPN) gateways not configured with multi-factor authentication (MFA)\r\n\r\n\r\nT1083\r\nDiscovery\r\nFile and Directory Discovery\r\nEnumerates files and encrypts all found\r\n\r\n\r\nT1078\r\nDefense Evasion, Initial Access, Persistence, Privilege Escalation\r\nValid Accounts\r\nUses legitimate VPN credentials or password dumps\r\n\r\n\r\nT1071\r\nCommand and Control\r\nApplication Layer Protocol\r\nUses multiple protocols alongside the Cobalt Strike post-exploitation framework\r\n\r\n\r\nT1059.007\r\nExecution\r\nCommand and Scripting Interpreter: JavaScript\r\nWscript makes an external connection upon executing a JavaScript file\r\n\r\n\r\nT1059.001\r\nExecution\r\nCommand and Scripting Interpreter: PowerShell\r\nUses the default PowerShell string for command execution on a remote host\r\n\r\n\r\nT1057\r\nDiscovery\r\nProcess Discovery\r\nThe Windows Restart Manager (rstrtmgr.dll) is used to identify processes using files that would prevent encryption, terminating anything that isn't a critical process\r\n\r\n\r\nT1048\r\nExfiltration\r\nExfiltration Over Alternative Protocol\r\nRclone is sometimes renamed to svchost.exe prior to execution and exfiltration over alternative protocols\r\n\r\n\r\nT1047\r\nExecution\r\nWindows Management Instrumentation\r\nImpacket framework execution relating to wmiexec; uses WMIC to load the ransomware as a library\r\n\r\n\r\nT1036\r\nDefense Evasion\r\nMasquerading\r\nRenaming PE files (e.g., Rclone.exe to 1.exe)\r\n\r\n\r\nT1027.007\r\nDefense Evasion\r\nObfuscated Files or Information: Dynamic API Resolution\r\nUses dynamic API resolution to conceal functionality\r\n\r\n\r\nT1021.002\r\nLateral Movement\r\nRemote Services: SMB\/Windows Admin Shares\r\nCopies the ransomware payload from VMs using PSExec to numerous hosts using SMB\r\n\r\n\r\nT1021.001\r\nLateral Movement\r\nRemote Services: Remote Desktop Protocol\r\nUses remote desktop protocol (RDP) for lateral movement\r\n\r\n\r\nT1003.006\r\nCredential Access\r\nOS Credential Dumping: DCSync\r\nConducts a DCSync attack for credential access\r\n\r\n\r\nT1003.003\r\nCredential Access\r\nOS Credential Dumping: NTDS\r\nUses ntdsutil.exe to dump Active Directory database\r\n\r\n\r\nT1003.001\r\nCredential Access\r\nOS Credential Dumping: LSASS Memory\r\nLSASS dumped via the Task Manager\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nTable 2. MITRE ATT&amp;CK techniques.\r\nXDR Query Language (XQL) Queries\r\nThis section documents relevant TTPs used by Ignoble Scorpius and maps them directly to Palo Alto Networks Cortex XQL queries. These queries detect renamed tools with Cortex XDR.\r\n\r\nLike many ransomware actors, Ignoble Scorpius likes to rename their Portable Executable (PEs) files. For example, rather than execute a tool such as Rclone as rclone.exe, the actor might rename it to something else, such as svchost.exe.\r\n\r\nIn the case mentioned above, a query for action_process_image_name = \u201crclone.exe\u201d in Cortex XDR\u2019s Query Language (XQL) will fail. However, Cortex XDR can identify these files even if they\u2019ve been renamed.\r\n\r\nWhen a PE is compiled, it often includes a resource called VERSIONINFO. This resource can contain the original file name, the company that produced the software, and more. Though ransomware actors can rename executables, they rarely alter the VERSIONINFO resource.\r\n\r\nWe can extract the VERSIONINFO from PEs that run on a host using Cortex XDR with the action_process_file_info field in the ENUM.PROCESS filter set, shown in the following XQL query snippet.\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\r\n\r\n| filter event_type = ENUM.PROCESS and event_sub_type = ENUM.PROCESS_START\r\n\r\n| alter\r\n\r\naction_process_original_name = action_process_file_info -&gt; original_name,\r\n\r\naction_process_company_name = action_process_file_info -&gt; company,\r\n\r\naction_process_description = action_process_file_info -&gt; description,\r\n\r\naction_process_internal_name = action_process_file_info -&gt; internal_name,\r\n\r\naction_process_legal_copyright = action_process_file_info -&gt; legal_copyright\r\nTable 3 below highlights data from the VERSIONINFO resource, which is extracted for running processes by the above query.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nVERSIONINFO Data\r\nDescription\r\n\r\n\r\noriginal_name\r\nThe original name of a PE upon compilation\r\n\r\n\r\ncompany\r\nThe company that released the software\r\n\r\n\r\ndescription\r\nA description of the compiled software\r\n\r\n\r\ninternal_name\r\nThe internal name of the PE. This is often equal to or very similar to the original_name.\r\n\r\n\r\nlegal_copyright\r\nA copyright notification from the releasing company\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nTable 3. Ignoble Scorpius data extraction.\r\n\r\nOnce the VERSIONINFO data has been extracted, XQL can then be used to filter on known version info values from executables. The following is an example filter set that will identify renamed versions of Rclone\u2019s default executable, rclone.exe.\r\n| filter\u00a0\r\n\r\n(action_process_image_name = \"rclone.exe\" or\u00a0\r\n\r\naction_process_original_name ~= \"rclone\" or\u00a0\r\n\r\naction_process_company_name ~= \"https\\:\\\/\\\/rclone\\.org\" or\u00a0\r\n\r\naction_process_description ~= \"rclone\" or\u00a0\r\n\r\naction_process_internal_name ~= \"rclone\" or\r\n\r\naction_process_legal_copyright = \"The Rclone Authors\")\r\nSome of the Cortex XDR queries we\u2019ve included in this report use the above method for identifying renamed executables.\r\n1. GootLoader: Wscript Making External Connection\r\nTechnique description: The query looks for wscript.exe making external connections upon executing a JavaScript (.js) file, which could be indicative of GootLoader activity. The query restricts results to user-based Downloads or Temp folders, as these are the directories most commonly associated with GootLoader infections.\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTP ID\r\n\r\n \tT1059.007 Execution - Command and Scripting Interpreter: JavaScript\r\n\r\nXQL Query\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false timeframe = 30d\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\r\n\r\n| filter event_type = ENUM.STORY and agent_os_type = ENUM.AGENT_OS_WINDOWS\r\n\r\n| filter actor_process_image_name\u00a0 = \"wscript.exe\" and actor_process_command_line\u00a0 contains \".js\"\r\n\r\n| filter actor_process_command_line contains \"\\Users\\*\\Downloads\" or actor_process_command_line contains \"\\Users\\*\\Temp\"\r\n\r\n| filter dst_is_internal_ip = False\r\n\r\n| fields _time, agent_hostname, actor_effective_username,actor_process_image_name, actor_process_command_line, action_remote_ip, dst_action_external_hostname\r\n\r\n| sort desc _time\r\n2. Dumping LSASS via Task Manager\r\nTechnique description: The query looks for LSASS being dumped via the Task Manager. To identify this activity, we focus on lsass.DMP files being created via the Taskmgr.exe process.\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTP ID\r\n\r\n \tT1003.001 Credential Access - OS Credential Dumping: LSASS Memory\r\n\r\nXQL Query\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false timeframe = 30d\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\r\n\r\n| filter event_type = ENUM.FILE and event_sub_type = ENUM.FILE_CREATE_NEW and agent_os_type = ENUM.AGENT_OS_WINDOWS\r\n\r\n| filter action_file_name = \"lsass.DMP\" and actor_process_image_name = \"Taskmgr.exe\"\r\n\r\n| fields agent_hostname, event_type, event_sub_type, action_file_name, action_file_path, action_file_sha256, action_file_md5, actor_process_image_name, actor_process_image_path, actor_process_image_command_line\r\n\r\n| sort desc _time\r\n3. Impacket Process Execution\r\nTechnique description: The query looks for signs of Impacket framework execution, especially relating to smbexec and wmiexec. It focuses on the default PowerShell string used for command execution on the remote host.\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTP IDs\r\n\r\n \tT1059.001 Execution - Command and Scripting Interpreter: PowerShell\r\n \tT1047 Execution - Windows Management Instrumentation\r\n\r\nXQL Query\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false timeframe = 30d\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\r\n\r\n| filter event_type = ENUM.PROCESS and agent_os_type = ENUM.AGENT_OS_WINDOWS\r\n\r\n| filter (causality_actor_process_image_name = \"wmiprvse.exe\" or causality_actor_process_image_name = \"services.exe\") and actor_process_image_name = \"powershell.exe\"\r\n\r\n| filter actor_process_command_line ~= \"-NoP -NoL -sta -NonI -W Hidden -Exec Bypass -Enc\"\r\n\r\n| sort desc _time\r\n4. Mimikatz and Rubeus Execution\r\nTechnique description: The query looks for signs of Mimiktaz or Rubeus executing within the environment. It takes into account renamed process image files by using PE metadata to identify VERSIONINFO data of executing processes.\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTP ID\r\n\r\n \tT1003.001 Credential Access - OS Credential Dumping: LSASS Memory\r\n\r\nXQL Query\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false timeframe = 30d\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\u00a0\r\n\r\n| filter event_type = ENUM.PROCESS and event_sub_type = ENUM.PROCESS_START and agent_os_type = ENUM.AGENT_OS_WINDOWS\r\n\r\n| alter\u00a0\r\n\r\naction_process_original_name = action_process_file_info -&gt; original_name,\r\n\r\naction_process_company_name = action_process_file_info -&gt; company,\r\n\r\naction_process_description = action_process_file_info -&gt; description,\r\n\r\naction_process_internal_name = action_process_file_info -&gt; internal_name,\r\n\r\naction_process_legal_copyright = action_process_file_info -&gt; legal_copyright\r\n\r\n| filter (action_process_image_name ~= \"(mimikatz|rubeus)\\.exe\" or action_process_original_name ~= \"(mimikatz|rubeus)\" or action_process_description ~= \"(mimikatz|rubeus)\" or action_process_internal_name ~= \"(mimikatz|rubeus)\")\r\n\r\n| fields _time, agent_hostname, agent_ip_addresses, actor_effective_username, action_process_image_name, action_process_image_path, action_process_image_command_line, action_process_image_sha256, actor_process_image_name, actor_process_image_path, actor_process_command_line, actor_process_image_sha256, os_actor_process_command_line, action_process_original_name, action_process_company_name, action_process_description, action_process_internal_name, action_process_legal_copyright, action_process_file_info\r\n\r\n| sort desc _time\r\n5. Active Directory Dumping via NTDSUTIL\r\nTechnique description: The query looks for the use of ntdsutil.exe to dump the Active Directory database (NTDS.dit).\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTP ID\r\n\r\n \tCredential Access - T1003.003 OS Credential Dumping: NTDS\r\n\r\nXQL Query\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false timeframe = 30d\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\r\n\r\n| filter event_type = ENUM.PROCESS and event_sub_type = ENUM.PROCESS_START and agent_os_type = ENUM.AGENT_OS_WINDOWS\r\n\r\n| filter action_process_image_name = \"ntdsutil.exe\" and (action_process_image_command_line contains \"ac i ntds\" or action_process_image_command_line contains \"activate instance ntds\") and action_process_image_command_line contains \"create full\"\r\n\r\n| fields _time, agent_hostname, agent_ip_addresses, actor_effective_username, action_process_image_name, action_process_image_path, action_process_image_command_line, action_process_image_sha256, actor_process_image_name, actor_process_image_path, actor_process_command_line, actor_process_image_sha256, os_actor_process_command_line, action_process_file_info\r\n\r\n| sort desc _time\r\n6. Cobalt Strike Combined Query\r\nTechnique description: The query looks for a combination of identifiers related to the Cobalt Strike post-exploitation framework. Though the tool is used legitimately by pentesting, red teaming and emulation teams alike, threat actors such as BlackSuit also like to use the tool.\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTP ID\r\n\r\n \tT1071 Command and Control - Application Layer Protocol\r\n\r\nXQL Query\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false timeframe = 30d\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\u00a0\r\n\r\n| filter (event_type = ENUM.PROCESS AND event_sub_type = ENUM.PROCESS_START and actor_process_image_name = \"services.exe\" and action_process_image_command_line ~= \".+\\\\admin\\$\\\\[a-z0-9]{7}\\.exe\")\r\n\r\nor (event_type = ENUM.PROCESS AND event_sub_type = ENUM.PROCESS_START and (action_process_image_command_line = \"c:\\windows\\system32\\rundll32.exe\" or action_process_image_command_line = \"c:\\windows\\syswow64\\rundll32.exe\" and actor_process_image_name != \"setup.exe\" and actor_process_command_line not contains \"chrome\" and actor_process_command_line not contains \"edge\"))\r\n\r\nor (event_type = ENUM.FILE and action_file_path ~= \"\\\\device\\\\namedpipe\\\\msse-\\d+-server\" or action_file_path ~= \"\\\\device\\\\namedpipe\\\\postex_[a-z0-9]{4}\" or action_file_path ~= \"\\\\device\\\\namedpipe\\\\status_[a-z0-9]{4}\" or action_file_path ~= \"\\\\device\\\\namedpipe\\\\msagent_[a-z0-9]{4}\")\r\n\r\nor (event_type = ENUM.PROCESS AND event_sub_type = ENUM.PROCESS_START and (action_process_image_name contains \"powershell.exe\" OR actor_process_image_name contains \"cmd.exe\") AND ((action_process_image_command_line contains \"-enc jabzad0\" OR action_process_image_command_line contains \"-encodedcommand jabzad0\")))\r\n\r\nor (event_type = ENUM.STORY and dst_action_external_hostname contains \"aaa.stage\")\r\n\r\nor (event_type = ENUM.EVENT_LOG and (action_evtlog_message ~= \"\\$s=New-Object IO.MemoryStream\" OR action_evtlog_message ~= \"\\$var_code\"))\r\n\r\n| fields agent_hostname, agent_id, agent_ip_addresses , agent_version, actor_effective_username, actor_process_image_name, actor_process_image_path, actor_process_command_line, action_process_image_command_line, action_file_path, action_evtlog_username, action_evtlog_message, actor_process_signature_vendor\r\n\r\n| filter not ((actor_process_image_path contains \"Microsoft\\EdgeWebView\\Application\" or actor_process_image_path contains \"Microsoft\\EdgeUpdate\\Install\" or actor_process_image_path contains \"Microsoft\\Edge\\Application\" or actor_process_image_path contains \"Chromium\" or actor_process_image_path contains \"Installer\\setup.exe\") and (actor_process_signature_vendor = \"Microsoft Corporation\" or actor_process_image_name = \"setup.exe\"))\r\n\r\n| sort desc _time\r\n7. Rclone Exfiltration\r\nTechnique description: The query looks for data exfiltration via Rclone, a tool used by BlackSuit to exfiltrate data from victim environments. It takes into account renamed process image files by using PE metadata to identify VERSIONINFO data of executing processes.\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTP IDs\r\n\r\n \tT1567 Exfiltration - Exfiltration Over Web Service\r\n\r\nXQL Query\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false timeframe = 30d\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\u00a0\r\n\r\n| filter event_type = ENUM.PROCESS and event_sub_type = ENUM.PROCESS_START and agent_os_type = ENUM.AGENT_OS_WINDOWS\r\n\r\n| alter\u00a0\r\n\r\naction_process_original_name = action_process_file_info -&gt; original_name,\r\n\r\naction_process_company_name = action_process_file_info -&gt; company,\r\n\r\naction_process_description = action_process_file_info -&gt; description,\r\n\r\naction_process_internal_name = action_process_file_info -&gt; internal_name,\r\n\r\naction_process_legal_copyright = action_process_file_info -&gt; legal_copyright\r\n\r\n| filter\u00a0\r\n\r\n(action_process_image_name = \"rclone.exe\" or\u00a0\r\n\r\naction_process_original_name ~= \"rclone\" or\u00a0\r\n\r\naction_process_company_name ~= \"https\\:\\\/\\\/rclone\\.org\" or\u00a0\r\n\r\naction_process_description ~= \"rclone\" or\u00a0\r\n\r\naction_process_internal_name ~= \"rclone\" or\r\n\r\naction_process_legal_copyright = \"The Rclone Authors\") and\u00a0\r\n\r\naction_process_image_command_line in (\"*lsd*\", \"*remote:*\", \"*mega*\", \"*--config*\", \"*--auto-confirm*\", \"*or\u00a0 --multi-thread-streams and copy*\", \"*config*\", \"*create*\", \"*user*\", \"*pass*\", \"*progress*\", \"*no-check-certificate*\", \"*ignore-existing*\", \"*auto-confirm*\", \"*multi-thread-streams*\", \"*transfers*\", \"*ftp:*\")\r\n\r\n| fields _time, agent_hostname, agent_ip_addresses, actor_effective_username, action_process_image_name, action_process_image_path, action_process_image_command_line, action_process_image_sha256, actor_process_image_name, actor_process_image_path, actor_process_command_line, actor_process_image_sha256, os_actor_process_command_line\r\n\r\n| sort desc _time\r\n8. Shadow Copy Deletion via VSSADMIN\r\nTechnique description: The query looks for deletion of shadow copies using a specific vssadmin.exe command associated with the BlackSuit encryptor.\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTP IDs\r\n\r\n \tT1490 Impact - Inhibit System Recovery\r\n\r\nXQL Query\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false timeframe = 30d\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\r\n\r\n| filter event_type = ENUM.PROCESS and event_sub_type = ENUM.PROCESS_START and agent_os_type = ENUM.AGENT_OS_WINDOWS\r\n\r\n| filter action_process_image_command_line ~= \"cmd.exe\\s+\\\/c\\svssadmin\\sdelete\\sshadows\\s\\\/all\\s\\\/quiet\" or actor_process_image_command_line ~= \"cmd.exe\\s+\\\/c\\svssadmin\\sdelete\\sshadows\\s\\\/all\\s\\\/quiet\"\r\n\r\n| fields _time, agent_hostname, agent_ip_addresses, actor_effective_username, action_process_image_name, action_process_image_path, action_process_image_command_line, action_process_image_sha256, actor_process_image_name, actor_process_image_path, actor_process_command_line, actor_process_image_sha256, os_actor_process_command_line, action_process_file_info\r\n\r\n| sort desc _time\r\n9. BlackSuit Mutex\r\nTechnique description: The query looks for the mutex created by the BlackSuit encryptor. This mutex is created and checked upon execution to ensure no more than a single encryptor runs at one time.\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTP ID\r\n\r\n \tT1027 Execution - Obfuscated Files or Information\r\n\r\nXQL Query\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false timeframe = 30d\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\r\n\r\n| filter event_type = ENUM.SYSTEM_CALL and event_sub_type = ENUM.SYSTEM_CALL_NT_CREATE_MUTANT and agent_os_type = ENUM.AGENT_OS_WINDOWS\r\n\r\n| fields agent_hostname, action_syscall_string_params\u00a0\r\n\r\n| alter syscall_mutant_name = json_extract(action_syscall_string_params, \"$.1\")\r\n\r\n| alter syscall_mutant_name = trim(to_string(syscall_mutant_name),\"\\\"\")\r\n\r\n| filter syscall_mutant_name ~= \"WLm87eV1oNRx6P3E4Cy9\"\r\n\r\n| sort desc _time\r\n10. BlackSuit Encrypted Files\r\nTechnique description: The query looks for files encrypted with the .blacksuit file suffix, which indicates the BlackSuit encryptor has encrypted the file.\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTP ID\r\n\r\n \tT1486 Impact - Data Encrypted for Impact\r\n\r\nXQL Query\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false timeframe = 30d\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\r\n\r\n| filter event_type = ENUM.FILE and action_file_extension ~= \"blacksuit\"\r\n\r\n| fields agent_hostname, event_type, event_sub_type, action_file_name, action_file_path, action_file_sha256, action_file_md5, actor_process_image_name, actor_process_image_path, actor_process_image_command_line\r\n11. BlackSuit Ransom Note\r\nTechnique description: The query looks for known names of the BlackSuit encryptor\u2019s ransomware notes.\r\nMITRE ATT&amp;CK TTP ID\r\n\r\n \tT1486 Impact - Data Encrypted for Impact\r\n\r\nXQL Query\r\nconfig case_sensitive = false timeframe = 30d\r\n\r\n| dataset = xdr_data\r\n\r\n| filter event_type = ENUM.FILE and event_sub_type = ENUM.FILE_CREATE_NEW and action_file_name ~= \"README.BlackSuit.txt\"\r\n\r\n| fields agent_hostname, event_type, event_sub_type, action_file_name, action_file_path, action_file_sha256, action_file_md5, actor_process_image_name, actor_process_image_path, actor_process_image_command_line","publisher":{"@type":"Organization","@id":"#panworg"},"image":{"@type":"ImageObject","url":"https:\/\/unit42.paloaltonetworks.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2024\/11\/04_Ransomware_Category_1920x900-300x300.jpg","width":300,"height":300},"speakable":{"@type":"SpeakableSpecification","xPath":["\/html\/head\/title","\/html\/head\/meta[@name='description']\/@content"]},"author":[{"@type":"Person","name":"Unit 42"}]}</script><link rel='stylesheet' id='crayon-css' href='https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/plugins/crayon-syntax-highlighter/css/min/crayon.min.css?ver=_2.7.2_beta' media='all' />

    ;(function(win, doc, style, timeout) {
    var STYLE_ID = 'at-body-style';
    function getParent() {
    return doc.getElementsByTagName('head')[0];
    }
    function addStyle(parent, id, def) {
        if (!parent) {
        return;
        }
        var style = doc.createElement('style');
        style.id = id;
        style.innerHTML = def;
        parent.appendChild(style);
    }
    function removeStyle(parent, id) {
        if (!parent) {
            return;
        }
        var style = doc.getElementById(id);
        if (!style) {
            return;
        }
        parent.removeChild(style);
    }
    addStyle(getParent(), STYLE_ID, style);
    setTimeout(function() {
    removeStyle(getParent(), STYLE_ID);
    }, timeout);
    }(window, document, "body {visibility:hidden !important}", 3000));

    /**
 * String.prototype.replaceAll() polyfill
 * https://gomakethings.com/how-to-replace-a-section-of-a-string-with-another-one-with-vanilla-js/
 * @author Chris Ferdinandi
 * @license MIT
 */
if (!String.prototype.replaceAll) {
	String.prototype.replaceAll = function(str, newStr){
		// If a regex pattern
		if (Object.prototype.toString.call(str).toLowerCase() === '[object regexp]') {
			return this.replace(str, newStr);
		}
		// If a string
		return this.replace(new RegExp(str, 'g'), newStr);
	};

	function getCookie(cname) {
	 	var name = cname + "=";
  		var decodedCookie = decodeURIComponent(document.cookie);
		var ca = decodedCookie.split(';');
  		for(var i = 0; i <ca.length; i++) {
    			var c = ca[i];
    			while (c.charAt(0) == ' ') {
     				 c = c.substring(1);
    			}
    			if (c.indexOf(name) == 0) {
    				 return c.substring(name.length, c.length);
    			}
  		}
  		return "";
	}

	var referer = "";//sessionStorage.container;
	var pcontainer = sessionStorage.getItem("container");
	var searchResultsPagePath = "";
	if(((pcontainer) && pcontainer.indexOf('Prisma')!=-1)){
	    referer = 'Prisma' ;
	}
        else if(((pcontainer) && pcontainer.indexOf('Cortex')!=-1)){
	    referer = 'Cortex' ;
	}
        else if(((pcontainer) && pcontainer.indexOf('Sase')!=-1)){
	    referer = 'Sase' ;
	}
	else if(((pcontainer) && pcontainer.indexOf('Unit')!=-1)){
	    referer = 'Unit' ;
	}
	else if(((pcontainer) && pcontainer.indexOf('Ngfw')!=-1)){
	    referer = 'Ngfw' ;
	}
        var fromRef = document.referrer;
        var nContainer = getCookie("navContainer");
        if(nContainer){//If user is coming from main site, we need to reset the container		
		if(fromRef  && fromRef.indexOf("prismacloud.io")!=-1){
                        referer = 'Prisma' ;
                        sessionStorage.setItem("container","Prisma");
                } else if(fromRef.indexOf("paloaltonetworks.com")!=-1 || fromRef.indexOf("paloaltonetworks.jp")!=-1 ){
                        if(nContainer.indexOf('Prisma') != -1){
                            referer = 'Prisma' ;
                            sessionStorage.setItem("container","Prisma");
                        }
                        if(nContainer.indexOf('Cortex') != -1){
                            referer = 'Cortex' ;
                            sessionStorage.setItem("container","Cortex");
                        }
			if(nContainer.indexOf('Sase') != -1){
                            referer = 'Sase' ;
                            sessionStorage.setItem("container","Sase");
                        }
			if(nContainer.indexOf('Unit') != -1){
                            referer = 'Unit' ;
                            sessionStorage.setItem("container","Unit");
                        }
			if(nContainer.indexOf('Ngfw') != -1){
                            referer = 'Ngfw' ;
                            sessionStorage.setItem("container","Ngfw");
                        }
			document.cookie = 'navContainer=; path=/; domain=.paloaltonetworks.com; expires=' + new Date(0).toUTCString();
		}
	}
if(referer != "Prisma" && referer != "Cortex" && referer != "Sase" && referer != "Unit" && referer != "Ngfw") {
    referer = 'Unit' ;
    sessionStorage.setItem("container","Unit");
}
function callMainSitePrismaNavHTML(){
    
    var referrer_domain = 'https://www.paloaltonetworks.com';
    sessionStorage.setItem("domain",referrer_domain);
    if(referer == 'Prisma'){
        var menu_url = referrer_domain+'/_jcr_content/globals/cleanHeaderPrisma.prismaRenderer.html';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/prismasearch";
        }
    if(referer == 'Cortex'){
        var menu_url = referrer_domain+'/_jcr_content/globals/cleanHeaderCortex.cortexRenderer.html';	
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/cortexsearch";	
    }
    if(referer == 'Sase'){
        var menu_url = referrer_domain+'/_jcr_content/globals/cleanHeaderSase.saseRenderer.html';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/sasesearch";
    }
    if(referer == 'Unit'){
        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/unit-nav-renderer.php';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/content/pan/en_US/search/unit42search";
		    }
    if(referer == 'Ngfw'){
        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/ngfw-cdss-nav-renderer.php';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/ngfwcdsssearch";
    }
    httpGet(menu_url,'menu_html');
    document.getElementById('main-nav-menu-cont').removeAttribute("style");
}
function addStyle(styles) {            
    /* Create style document */
    var css = document.createElement('style');
    css.type = 'text/css';

    if (css.styleSheet) 
        css.styleSheet.cssText = styles;
    else 
        css.appendChild(document.createTextNode(styles));

    /* Append style to the tag name */
    document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(css);
}
function httpGet(theUrl,req_type) {
    if (window.XMLHttpRequest) { // code for IE7+, Firefox, Chrome, Opera, Safari
        xmlhttp=new XMLHttpRequest();
    } else {// code for IE6, IE5
        xmlhttp=new ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
    }
    xmlhttp.onreadystatechange=function()
    {
        if (xmlhttp.readyState==4 && xmlhttp.status==200)
        {
            if(req_type == 'menu_html'){
            var nav_text = xmlhttp.responseText.replaceAll('https://static.cloud.coveo.com/searchui/v2.9159/js/CoveoJsSearch.Lazy.min.js', '');
            nav_text = nav_text.replaceAll('src="/', 'src="'+maindomain_lang+'/');
            nav_text = nav_text.replaceAll("'/content", "'"+maindomain_lang+"/content");
                        
            document.getElementById("PAN_2021_NAV_ASYNC").innerHTML = nav_text.replaceAll('href="/', 'href="'+maindomain_lang+'/');

            var lozad_back = document.getElementsByClassName('lozad-background');
            Array.prototype.forEach.call(lozad_back, function(el) {
            // Do stuff here
            var el_back_img_path = el.getAttribute('data-background-image');
            var first_pos = el_back_img_path.indexOf("'");
            var last_pos = el_back_img_path.indexOf("'",first_pos+1);
            el_back_img_path = el_back_img_path.substring(first_pos+1,last_pos);
            el.setAttribute("data-background-image",main_site_url+el_back_img_path);
            });
            }
            if(req_type == 'head_inline_css'){
            addStyle(xmlhttp.responseText);
            }
        }
    }
    xmlhttp.open("GET", theUrl, true );
    xmlhttp.send();    
}    
    
if(referer == 'Prisma' || referer == 'Cortex' || referer == 'Sase' || referer == 'Unit' || referer == 'Ngfw'){
    const article = document.querySelector('#PAN_2021_NAV_ASYNC');
    if(referer == 'Prisma'){
        article.dataset.type = 'prisma';
        $('#PAN_2021_NAV_ASYNC').removeClass('default').addClass('defaultRedesigned');
    }
    else if(referer == 'Cortex'){
        article.dataset.type = 'cortex';
    }
    else if(referer == 'Sase'){
        article.dataset.type = 'sase';
    }
    else if(referer == 'Unit'){
        article.dataset.type = 'unit';
    }
    else if(referer == 'Ngfw'){
        article.dataset.type = 'ngfw';
    }
    //set class to default
    if(referer == 'Unit' || referer == 'Ngfw'){
        $('#PAN_2021_NAV_ASYNC').removeClass('default').addClass('defaultRedesigned');
    }
    callMainSitePrismaNavHTML();        
}

                <h2><a id="post-137574-_n41yi9jwwr88"></a>Executive Summary</h2>
<p>Unit 42 researchers have observed an increase in BlackSuit ransomware activity beginning in March 2024 that suggests a ramp up of operations. This threat emerged as a rebrand of Royal ransomware, which occurred in May 2023. Unit 42 tracks the group behind this threat as Ignoble Scorpius. Since the rebrand, Unit 42 has observed at least <strong>93</strong> victims globally, a quarter of which were in the construction and manufacturing industries.</p>
<p>The group describes themselves as an “extortioner named BlackSuit” and claims to reverse file encryption for “quite a small compensation essentially.” Although the group states the compensation is small, Unit 42 has observed that, on average, the initial ransom demand is about equal to <strong>1.6%</strong> of the victim organization’s annual revenue. As of the date of this report, the median victim revenue across all industries is roughly <strong>$19.5 million</strong>, making the ransom payout quite significant for all organizations.</p>
<p>This threat assessment includes details identified during routine threat research activities, incident response cases and collaboration with the Unit 42 Managed Threat Hunting team.</p>
<p>This report maps the group’s activity to the MITRE ATT&amp;CK® framework in <a href="#post-137574-_pa5s1ucxb5t">that section</a>, which organizations can use to assess their coverage of threats posed by Ignoble Scorpius, pre- and post-compromise.</p>
<p>Palo Alto Networks customers are better protected from the threats discussed above through the following products:</p>
<ul>
<li>The Unit 42 <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/unit42/respond/managed-threat-hunting" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Managed Threat Hunting</a> and <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/resources/datasheets/unit42-managed-detection-and-response" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Managed Detection and Response</a> teams conduct proactive hunts for pre- and post-incident activity.</li>
<li><a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/resources/datasheets/cortex-xdr" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Cortex XDR</a> and <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/resources/datasheets/cortex-xsiam-aag" target="_blank" rel="noopener">XSIAM</a> block and alert on known techniques and files associated with Ignoble Scorpius. We provide XQL queries in the <a href="#post-137574-_pa5s1ucxb5t">MITRE ATT&amp;CK TTPs section</a> of this report.</li>
<li>Palo Alto Networks <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/network-security/next-generation-firewall" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Next-Generation Firewalls</a> with <a href="https://www.paloaltonetworks.com/network-security/security-subscriptions" target="_blank" rel="noopener">cloud-delivered security services</a>, including <a href="https://docs.paloaltonetworks.com/advanced-wildfire" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Advanced WildFire</a>, detect known malicious files associated with Ignoble Scorpius.</li>
<li>Organizations can engage the <a href="https://start.paloaltonetworks.com/contact-unit42.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Unit 42 Incident Response team</a> to help with a compromise or to provide a proactive assessment to lower your risk.</li>
</ul>

<h2><a id="post-137574-_7j1607r4zj9m"></a>BlackSuit Ransomware Overview</h2>
<p>BlackSuit ransomware emerged in May 2023 as a <a href="https://www.cisa.gov/news-events/cybersecurity-advisories/aa23-061a" target="_blank" rel="noopener">rebrand of the Royal ransomware</a>. Unit 42 Threat Intelligence assesses that the group behind this threat is a direct evolution of <a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/royal-ransomware/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Royal</a>, and as such we track the group under the same moniker, Ignoble Scorpius.</p>
<p>Much like the operations as Royal ransomware, BlackSuit operates a dark web leak site where they publish their victims’ names and stolen data to extort them into paying a ransom. Figure 1 shows an excerpt of this site.</p>
<figure id="attachment_137589" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-137589" style="width: 1999px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-137589 size-full lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/image6.jpg" alt="Screenshot of the BlackSuit ransomware leak site with much of the information redacted. The user has the ability to search the site. The text on the website talks about a company facing consequences after data was disclosed. " width="1999" height="1453" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/image6.jpg 1999w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/image6-605x440.jpg 605w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/image6-963x700.jpg 963w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/image6-768x558.jpg 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/image6-1536x1116.jpg 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 1999px) 100vw, 1999px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-137589" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 1. Screenshot of BlackSuit leak site.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Since the rebrand, Unit 42 has observed at least 93 victims globally and an upward trend in the number of successful compromises shared on their leak site. This suggests an overall ramping up of operations. Figure 2 below details the monthly total leak site posts from Ignoble Scorpius as BlackSuit.</p>
<figure id="attachment_137581" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-137581" style="width: 900px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-137581 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-116463-137574-3.png" alt="Bar chart of the number of leak site posts per month from May 2023 through October 2024. Activity peaks in May 2024." width="900" height="530" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-116463-137574-3.png 2048w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-116463-137574-3-747x440.png 747w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-116463-137574-3-1189x700.png 1189w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-116463-137574-3-768x452.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-116463-137574-3-1536x905.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-137581" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 2. Activity from Ignoble Scorpius under the BlackSuit name, May 2023 through October 2024.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The number of organizations truly impacted by the group is likely higher, as organizations can pay their ransom before ransomware operators post details on their leak sites to avoid reputational damage.</p>
<p>The median revenue of these victims was $19.5 million, which highlights the average size of organizations that the group has successfully targeted. Based on ransom negotiations observed by Unit 42, we can also estimate that the group’s initial ransom demand is equal to about 1.6% of the victim organization’s annual revenue.</p>
<p>Breaking down the 93 victims by sector indicates a preference for the education, construction and manufacturing sectors, as shown in Figure 3 below.</p>
<figure id="attachment_137583" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-137583" style="width: 900px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-137583 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-120193-137574-4.png" alt="A pie chart showing the percentages by industry affected by Ignoble Scorpius. Education is the largest at 14%, then construction at 12.5%, manufacturing at 11%, and wholesale and retail at 10%. " width="900" height="515" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-120193-137574-4.png 2048w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-120193-137574-4-770x440.png 770w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-120193-137574-4-1224x700.png 1224w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-120193-137574-4-768x439.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-120193-137574-4-1536x878.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-137583" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 3. Pie chart breakdown of Ignoble Scorpius victimology.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Finally, as with many ransomware groups, Ignoble Scorpius’ victims are overwhelmingly based in the United States, as shown below in Figure 4.</p>
<figure id="attachment_137585" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-137585" style="width: 900px" class="wp-caption alignnone"><img  class="wp-image-137585 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-123988-137574-5.png" alt="A column chart of the distribution of Ignoble Scorpius's victim count by country. The highest count is the United States at close to 50. The next countries at counts under 10 are the United Kingdom, Belgium, German, Italy, Australia and others. " width="900" height="555" data-srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-123988-137574-5.png 2048w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-123988-137574-5-713x440.png 713w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-123988-137574-5-1134x700.png 1134w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-123988-137574-5-768x474.png 768w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-123988-137574-5-1536x948.png 1536w" sizes="(max-width: 900px) 100vw, 900px" /><figcaption id="caption-attachment-137585" class="wp-caption-text">Figure 4. Ignoble Scorpius’ geographical impact.</figcaption></figure>
<h2><a id="post-137574-_dgfxry9r7u1e"></a>Attack Lifecycle</h2>
<p>The following sections highlight tactics, techniques and procedures (TTPs) observed from Ignoble Scorpius during BlackSuit incident response investigations Unit 42 conducted. Similar findings have also been shared by researchers at <a href="https://www.reliaquest.com/blog/blacksuit-attack-analysis/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">ReliaQuest</a> and <a href="https://thedfirreport.com/2024/08/26/blacksuit-ransomware/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">The DFIR Report</a>.</p>
<h3><a id="post-137574-_rvw7ks1rozea"></a>Initial Access</h3>
<p>Initial access for Ignoble Scorpius, and ransomware groups in general, can be highly varied due to the prevalence of initial access brokers (IABs) who sell stolen credentials or other forms of access to organizations. While some threat actors obtain initial access on their own, others require the expertise of IABs to gain entry into a compromised network.</p>
<p>During an incident response investigation, delineating between the TTPs of a suspected IAB or the ransomware group is not always possible. Within Ignoble Scorpius’ ransomware cases, Unit 42 has observed many different initial access methods, including:</p>
<ul>
<li>Phishing campaigns with malicious email attachments (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/001/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1566.001</a>);</li>
<li>SEO poisoning with <a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/javascript-malware-gootloader/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">GootLoader</a> (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1608/006/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1608.006</a>);</li>
<li>Using legitimate VPN credentials (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1078/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1078</a>), potentially obtained via social engineering and voice-based phishing (aka vishing) of executives (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1566/004/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1566.004</a>)</li>
<li>A software supply chain attack (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1195/002/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1195.002</a>).</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="post-137574-_m2c2r4pi9kpb"></a>Credential Access and Privilege Escalation</h3>
<p>Unit 42 has observed Ignoble Scorpius using common credential theft tools, such as Mimikatz and <a href="https://github.com/fortra/nanodump" target="_blank" rel="noopener">NanoDump</a>, which is “a flexible tool that creates a minidump of the LSASS process.” Techniques observed include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Dumping LSASS via Taskmgr (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/001/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1003.001</a>)</li>
<li>Performing a DCSync attack (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/006/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1003.006</a>)</li>
<li>Using Impacket to conduct an adversary-in-the-middle (AiTM) attack (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1557/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1557</a>)</li>
<li>Requesting Kerberos service tickets (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1558/002" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1558.002</a>)</li>
</ul>
<p>Once they have obtained sufficiently privileged accounts (i.e., domain administrator on Windows systems) Ignoble Scorpius has been observed dumping the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">NTDS.dit</span> file via <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">ntdsutil</span>, (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1003/003" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1003.003</a>) to compromise the domain controller.</p>
<h3><a id="post-137574-_yx54qp99ar9j"></a>Lateral Movement</h3>
<p>Unit 42 has observed Ignoble Scorpius making use of RDP (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/001" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1021.001</a>), SMB (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/002" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1021.002</a>) and PsExec (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1570" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1570</a>) to move laterally across systems.</p>
<h3><a id="post-137574-_oto110idzv98"></a>Defense Evasion</h3>
<p>Unit 42 has observed Ignoble Scorpius and other ransomware groups making use of a vulnerable driver and loader, which are called STONESTOP and POORTRY by <a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/hunting-attestation-signed-malware/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Mandiant</a>. They use these tools to disable and evade antivirus and EDR solutions (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1562/001" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1562.001</a>).</p>
<h3><a id="post-137574-_lg69ufkzm164"></a>Exfiltration</h3>
<p>Ignoble Scorpius has used various commonly available software and services to exfiltrate victim data. We observed WinRAR and 7-Zip being used to compress and stage files prior to exfiltration, after which attackers used WinSCP over FTP and Rclone to exfiltrate files. In at least one instance, attackers renamed Rclone to <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">svchost.exe</span> prior to execution (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1048" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1048</a>).</p>
<p>Unit 42 has also observed Ignoble Scorpius using a third-party project management application named <a href="https://www.bublup.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Bublup</a> to exfiltrate files (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1567</a>, <a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1567/002" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1567.002</a>). Threat actors often abuse, take advantage of or subvert legitimate products for malicious purposes. This does not imply that the legitimate product is flawed or malicious.</p>
<h3><a id="post-137574-_uiwzb1ic6f14"></a>Execution and Impact</h3>
<p>As Ignoble Scorpius' goal is to encrypt and ransom a victim’s files, the primary payload of their campaigns is the BlackSuit ransomware. During incident response investigations involving BlackSuit, Unit 42 has also observed attackers using other tools for persistent access and the execution of arbitrary commands.</p>
<p>These additional tools include <a href="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/tag/cobalt-strike/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Cobalt Strike</a> and <a href="https://www.kroll.com/en/insights/publications/cyber/inside-the-systembc-malware-server" target="_blank" rel="noopener">SystemBC</a>. In these cases it was not possible to identify whether Ignoble Scorpius or an IAB deployed the tools.</p>
<p>The final ransomware payload has Windows and Linux operating system variants with specific functionality to target VMware ESXi servers in some Linux variants.</p>
<h4><a id="post-137574-_otxlpchy82tw"></a>Windows Variant</h4>
<p>Unit 42’s analysis of the Windows variant found that the execution of the malware required the command-line argument <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">-id</span> followed by a 32-character value. The ID identifies the victim and grants access to a private chat room on Ignoble Scorpius' dark website to negotiate the ransom. They provide the ID to the victim via the ransom note. An example ransom note is shown below:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v_2.7.2_beta -->

		<div id="crayon-673ddee43bd03688964766" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

Good whatever time of day it is!

Your safety service did a really poor job of protecting your files against our professionals.

Extortioner named BlackSuit has attacked your system.

As a result all your essential files were encrypted and saved at a secure server for further use and publishing on the Web into the public realm.

Now we have all your files like: financial reports, intellectual property, accounting, law actions and complaints, personal files and so on and so forth.

We are able to solve this problem in one touch.

We (BlackSuit) are ready to give you an opportunity to get all the things back if you agree to make a deal with us.

You have a chance to get rid of all possible financial, legal, insurance and many others risks and problems for a quite small compensation.

You can have a safety review of your systems.

All your files will be decrypted, your data will be reset, your systems will stay in safe.

Contact us through TOR browser using the link:

<p>Other command-line arguments for the Windows variant of BlackSuit malware are shown below in Table 1.</p>
<table style="width: 100%;">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td style="text-align: center;"><b>Argument</b></td>
<td style="text-align: center;"><b>Functionality</b></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400; font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">-path</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">Specifies a target directory to encrypt</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400; font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">-id</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">Victim ID</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400; font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">-ep</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">Percentage of a file that should be encrypted</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400; font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">-localonly</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">Encrypts only the local system</span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400; font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">-networkonly</span></td>
<td><span style="font-weight: 400;">Encrypts file shares connected to the system</span></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p><span style="font-size: 10pt;">Table 1. BlackSuit Windows variant command-line arguments.</span></p>
<p>Analysis of BlackSuit ransomware from <a href="https://www.trendmicro.com/en_us/research/23/e/investigating-blacksuit-ransomwares-similarities-to-royal.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">TrendMicro</a> and <a href="https://www.sentinelone.com/anthology/blacksuit/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">SentinelOne</a> in 2023 identified more command-line flags than recent samples. This could be due to the ransomware group creating variants that target ESXi servers specifically, <a href="#post-137574-_39nw4kl81362">which we detail below</a>, or a consolidation of functionality.</p>
<p>After the initial execution, the malware creates a mutual exclusion flag (aka mutex) with the value <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">Global\WLm87eV1oNRx6P3E4Cy9</span> to prevent machines from being infected multiple times. As a result, the mutex chosen by Ignoble Scorpius needs to be a unique value that is not frequently changed. Unit 42 has observed attackers using this mutex as recently as June 2024, with open source highlighting its use as early as <a href="https://www.trendmicro.com/vinfo/us/threat-encyclopedia/malware/ransom.win32.blacksuit.ypdjb" target="_blank" rel="noopener">October 2023</a>.</p>
<p>To ensure the encryption of as many files as possible, the ransomware enumerates and terminates a list of known processes and services (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1057" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1057</a>). The ransomware also uses Windows Restart Manager (<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">rstrtmgr.dll</span>) to identify processes using files that would prevent encryption, terminating anything that isn't a critical process or the Windows File Explorer (<span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">explorer.exe</span>). This is a technique <a href="https://www.crowdstrike.com/blog/windows-restart-manager-part-1/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">commonly used by ransomware payloads</a>.</p>
<p>The malware uses the following command to delete shadow backups (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1490" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1490</a>):</p>
<p><img  class="alignnone wp-image-137587 lozad"  data-src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/word-image-127276-137574-6.png" alt="Screenshot of code snippet that deletes versions. " width="400" height="25" /></p>
<p>To execute the ransomware payload, researchers at <a href="https://www.reliaquest.com/blog/blacksuit-attack-analysis/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">ReliaQuest</a> observed Ignoble Scorpius downloading VirtualBox and creating a virtual machine (VM) (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1564/006" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1564.006</a>). They copied the ransomware payload from the VM using PsExec (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1570" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1570</a>) to “hundreds of hosts via SMB” (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1021/002" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1021.002</a>). They then used Windows Management Instrumentation Command-line (WMIC) to load the ransomware as a library to execute it. This is a technique that Unit 42 has also observed from the group (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1047" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1047</a>, <a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1218/010" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1218.010</a>).</p>
<p>They then enumerate available files (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1083/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1083</a>) and encrypt them using OpenSSL AES, adding the extension <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">.blacksuit</span> to the encrypted file’s name (<a href="https://attack.mitre.org/techniques/T1486" target="_blank" rel="noopener">T1486</a>).</p>
<h4><a id="post-137574-_39nw4kl81362"></a>ESXi Variant</h4>
<p>The ESXi variant, a Linux-based executable, targets virtual machines and introduces two more command-line flags:</p>
<ul>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">-vmkill</span> (shuts down virtual machines before encryption if set)</li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">-crypt_all</span></li>
</ul>
<p>If the <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">-crypt_all</span> flag is not set, the following files relating to VMware are encrypted:</p>
<ul>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">*.vmsd</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">*.vmx</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">*.vmxf</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">*.vmdk</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">*.vmem</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">*.vmsn</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">*.nvram</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">*.vmx~</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">*.vswp</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">*.vmtx</span></li>
<li><span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier, monospace;">*.vmss</span></li>
</ul>
<h2><a id="post-137574-_rt54on20d5fv"></a>Conclusion</h2>
<p>Our analysis indicates that BlackSuit is a direct continuation of the activity under Royal, and as such we have opted to continue tracking the group under the same identifier as Royal – Ignoble Scorpius. The true effectiveness of rebranding is difficult to quantify. However, it can offer ransomware groups a respite from the scrutiny of researchers, law enforcement and the media.</p>
<p>A more subtle effect of rebranding is the perception it can have on defenders. For example, BlackSuit’s predecessor Royal and their predecessor Conti were some of the most reported and sophisticated ransomware groups while active.</p>
<p>As a result, organizations who were looking to assess their exposure to ransomware at the time could have looked toward the most prolific ransomware groups and attempted to cater their defensive solutions toward them. Rebranding resets this perception, and if it is accompanied with a shift in the group’s TTPs, it can place defenders on their back foot.</p>
<p>This is one of the primary reasons we chose to highlight Ignoble Scorpius’ BlackSuit ransomware in this report. Although the group as BlackSuit might not yet reach the top 10 list of ransomware groups by number of compromises, this group has the following qualities:</p>
<ul>
<li>They conduct complex supply chain attacks</li>
<li>They exhibit a high level of sophistication compromising at least 93 organizations without a public-facing RaaS program</li>
<li>Their membership likely includes members from Conti and Royal ransomware</li>
</ul>
<p>This report maps the group’s activity to the MITRE ATT&amp;CK framework in the <a href="#post-137574-_pa5s1ucxb5t">that section</a> below. Organizations can use this information to assess their coverage of threats posed by Ignoble Scorpius, pre- and post-compromise.</p>
